</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar" style="padding:0 0.5em"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:South_Slavic_languages_sidebar" title="Template:South Slavic languages sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:South_Slavic_languages_sidebar" title="Template talk:South Slavic languages sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:South_Slavic_languages_sidebar" title="Special:EditPage/Template:South Slavic languages sidebar"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Bosnian</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/6\/6b\/En-us-Bosnian.ogg\/En-us-Bosnian.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;En-us-Bosnian.ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/6/6b/En-us-Bosnian.ogg/En-us-Bosnian.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Bosnian.ogg" title="File:En-us-Bosnian.ogg">ⓘ</a></sup></span></span>; <span title="Serbo-Croatian-language text"><i lang="sh-Latn">bosanski</i></span> / <span title="Serbo-Croatian-language text"><span lang="sh-Cyrl">босански</span></span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="sh-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">&#91;bɔ̌sanskiː&#93;</a></span>), sometimes referred to as <b>Bosniak language</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">standardized</a> <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)#Standard_varieties" title="Variety (linguistics)">variety</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">Serbo-Croatian</a> <a href="/wiki/Pluricentric_language" title="Pluricentric language">pluricentric language</a> mainly used by ethnic <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Bosnian is one of three such varieties considered official languages of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>. It is also an officially recognized minority language in <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MontenegroConstitution_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MontenegroConstitution-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bosnian uses both the <a href="/wiki/Gaj%27s_Latin_alphabet" title="Gaj&#39;s Latin alphabet">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Cyrillic alphabets</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Cyrillic-note_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cyrillic-note-3">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup> with Latin in everyday use.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It is notable among the <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">varieties</a> of Serbo-Croatian for a number of <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish" title="Ottoman Turkish">Ottoman Turkish</a> loanwords, largely due to the language's interaction with those cultures through <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Islam in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Islamic</a> ties.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bosnian is based on the most widespread dialect of Serbo-Croatian, <a href="/wiki/Shtokavian" title="Shtokavian">Shtokavian</a>, more specifically on <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Herzegovinian_dialect" title="Eastern Herzegovinian dialect">Eastern Herzegovinian</a>, which is also the basis of standard Croatian, Serbian and <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a> varieties. Therefore, the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Common_Language" title="Declaration on the Common Language">Declaration on the Common Language</a> of Croats, Serbs, Bosniaks and Montenegrins was issued in 2017 in Sarajevo.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Until the 1990s, the common language was called Serbo-Croatian<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and that term is still used in English, along with "Bosnian-Croatian-Montenegrin-Serbian" (BCMS), especially in diplomatic circles.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Cyrillic" title="Bosnian Cyrillic">Bosnian Cyrillic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">Serbo-Croatian</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Standardization">Standardization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Standardization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Azbuka_BH.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Azbuka_BH.svg/660px-Azbuka_BH.svg.png" decoding="async" width="660" height="59" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Azbuka_BH.svg/990px-Azbuka_BH.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Azbuka_BH.svg/1320px-Azbuka_BH.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="171" /></a><figcaption>Old Bosnian alphabets: <i><a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Cyrillic" title="Bosnian Cyrillic">bosančica</a></i> (top line) and <i><a href="/wiki/Arebica" title="Arebica">arebica</a></i> (bottom line), compared with contemporary <i><a href="/wiki/Gaj%27s_Latin_alphabet" title="Gaj&#39;s Latin alphabet">latinica</a></i> (middle line)</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm/220px--WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="220" height="165" data-durationhint="113" data-mwtitle="WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="480p.vp9.webm" data-width="640" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-width="640" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm.m3u8" type="application/vnd.apple.mpegurl" data-transcodekey="m3u8" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="320" data-height="240" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm.360p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="360p.vp9.webm" data-width="480" data-height="360" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/8d/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm/WIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="480" data-height="360" /><track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AWIKITONGUES-_Mirela_speaking_Bosnian.webm&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬" data-dir="ltr" /></video></span><figcaption>A Bosnian speaker, recorded in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg/220px-RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="336" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg/330px-RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg/440px-RacsunBosanskiJezik1827.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1334" data-file-height="2035" /></a><figcaption>School book of Latin and Bosnian, 1827</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg/220px-Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="356" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg/330px-Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg/440px-Gramatika_bosanskog_jezika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="532" data-file-height="862" /></a><figcaption>Bosnian Grammar, 1890</figcaption></figure>
<div style="clear:left;" class=""></div>
<p>Although Bosnians are, at the level of <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular idiom</a>, linguistically more homogeneous than either Serbians or Croatians, unlike those nations they failed to <a href="/wiki/Codification_(linguistics)" title="Codification (linguistics)">codify</a> a standard language in the 19th century, with at least two factors being decisive:
</p>
<ul><li>The Bosnian elite, as closely intertwined with Ottoman life, wrote predominantly in foreign (Arabic, Persian, Ottoman Turkish) languages.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_literature" title="Vernacular literature">Vernacular literature</a> written in Bosnian with the <a href="/wiki/Arebica" title="Arebica">Arebica</a> script was relatively thin and sparse.</li>
<li>The Bosnians' national emancipation lagged behind that of the Serbs and Croats and because denominational rather than cultural or linguistic issues played the pivotal role, a Bosnian language project did not arouse much interest or support amongst the intelligentsia of the time.</li></ul>
<p>The modern Bosnian standard took shape in the 1990s and 2000s. Lexically, Islamic-Oriental loanwords are more frequent; phonetically: the phoneme /x/ (letter <i>h</i>) is reinstated in many words as a distinct feature of <a href="/wiki/Nonstandard_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Nonstandard dialect">vernacular</a> Bosniak speech and language tradition; also, there are some changes in grammar, morphology and orthography that reflect the Bosniak pre-<a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> literary tradition, mainly that of the Bosniak renaissance at the beginning of the 20th century.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_and_recognition">Controversy and recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Controversy and recognition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_(14151146675).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_%2814151146675%29.jpg/220px-Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_%2814151146675%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_%2814151146675%29.jpg/330px-Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_%2814151146675%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_%2814151146675%29.jpg/440px-Political_correctness_in_Bosnia_%2814151146675%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="850" /></a><figcaption>A <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_packaging_warning_messages" title="Tobacco packaging warning messages">cigarette warning</a> "Smoking seriously harms you and others around you", ostensibly in three languages. The "Bosnian" and "Croatian" versions are identical and the "Serbian" one is a Cyrilic <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliteration</a> of the exact same text.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The name "Bosnian language" is a controversial issue for some <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, who also refer to it as the "Bosniak" language (<a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbo-Croatian language">Serbo-Croatian</a>: <i lang="sh">bošnjački</i> / <span title="Serbo-Croatian-language text"><span lang="sh">бошњачки</span></span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="sh-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">&#91;bǒʃɲaːtʃkiː&#93;</a></span>). Bosniak linguists however insist that the only legitimate name is "Bosnian" language (<span title="Bosnian-language text"><i lang="bs">bosanski</i></span>) and that that is the name that both Croats and Serbs should use. The controversy arises because the name "Bosnian" may seem to imply that it is the language of all Bosnians, while <a href="/wiki/Croats_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Croats of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnian Croats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Serbs of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Serbs</a> reject that designation for their idioms.
</p><p>The language is called <i>Bosnian language</i> in the 1995 <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Accords</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlexander2006409_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlexander2006409-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and is concluded by observers to have received legitimacy and international recognition at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a> (ISO),<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Board_on_Geographic_Names" title="United States Board on Geographic Names">United States Board on Geographic Names</a> (BGN) and the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Committee_on_Geographical_Names_for_British_Official_Use" title="Permanent Committee on Geographical Names for British Official Use">Permanent Committee on Geographical Names</a> (PCGN) recognize the Bosnian language. Furthermore, the status of the Bosnian language is also recognized by bodies such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> and translation and interpreting accreditation agencies,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> including internet translation services.
</p><p>Most English-speaking language encyclopedias (<a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> etc.)<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> register the language solely as "Bosnian" language. The <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> registered the language as "Bosnian" and gave it an ISO-number. The Slavic language institutes in English-speaking countries offer courses in "Bosnian" or "Bosnian/Croatian/Serbian" language, not in "Bosniak" language (e.g. Columbia,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Cornell,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Chicago,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Washington,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Kansas).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The same is the case in German-speaking countries, where the language is taught under the name <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Bosnisch</i></span>, not <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Bosniakisch</i></span> (e.g. Vienna,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Graz,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Trier)<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> with very few exceptions.
</p><p>Some Croatian linguists (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Zvonko_Kova%C4%8D&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zvonko Kovač (page does not exist)">Zvonko Kovač</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Pranjkovi%C4%87" title="Ivo Pranjković">Ivo Pranjković</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Josip_Sili%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Josip Silić (page does not exist)">Josip Silić</a>) support the name "Bosnian" language, whereas others (<a href="/wiki/Radoslav_Kati%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Radoslav Katičić">Radoslav Katičić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalibor_Brozovi%C4%87" title="Dalibor Brozović">Dalibor Brozović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Ladan" title="Tomislav Ladan">Tomislav Ladan</a>) hold that the term <i>Bosnian language</i> is the only one appropriate<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and that accordingly the terms Bosnian language and Bosniak language refer to two different things.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Croatian state institutions, such as the Central Bureau of Statistics, use both terms: "Bosniak" language was used in the 2001 census,<sup id="cite_ref-DZS_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DZS-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> while the census in 2011 used the term "Bosnian" language.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of Serbian linguists hold that the term <i>Bosniak language</i> is the only one appropriate,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> which was agreed as early as 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The original form of <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">The Constitution of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> called the language "Bosniac language",<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> until 2002 when it was changed in Amendment XXIX of the Constitution of the Federation by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Petritsch" title="Wolfgang Petritsch">Wolfgang Petritsch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The original text of the Constitution of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> was agreed in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and was signed by <a href="/wiki/Kre%C5%A1imir_Zubak" title="Krešimir Zubak">Krešimir Zubak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haris_Silajd%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Haris Silajdžić">Haris Silajdžić</a> on March 18, 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The constitution of <span title="Serbian-language text"><i lang="sr"><a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a></i></span>, the Serb-dominated entity within Bosnia and Herzegovina, did not recognize any language or ethnic group other than Serbian.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Bosniaks were mostly expelled from the territory controlled by the Serbs from 1992, but immediately after the war they demanded the restoration of their civil rights in those territories. The Bosnian Serbs refused to make reference to the Bosnian language in their constitution and as a result had constitutional amendments imposed by <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_for_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="High Representative for Bosnia and Herzegovina">High Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Petritsch" title="Wolfgang Petritsch">Wolfgang Petritsch</a>. However, the constitution of <span title="Serbian-language text"><i lang="sr">Republika Srpska</i></span> refers to it as the <i>Language spoken by Bosniaks</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> because the Serbs were required to recognise the language officially, but wished to avoid recognition of its name.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Serbia includes the Bosnian language as an elective subject in primary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> officially recognizes the Bosnian language: its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Montenegro" title="Constitution of Montenegro">2007 Constitution</a> specifically states that although <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a> is the official language, Serbian, Bosnian, Albanian and Croatian are also in official use.<sup id="cite_ref-MontenegroConstitution_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MontenegroConstitution-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_usage_of_the_term">Historical usage of the term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Historical usage of the term"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Cleanup-lang plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section should <b>specify the language</b> of its non-English content, using &#123;&#123;<a href="/wiki/Template:Lang" title="Template:Lang">lang</a>&#125;&#125;, &#123;&#123;<a href="/wiki/Template:Transliteration" title="Template:Transliteration">transliteration</a>&#125;&#125; for transliterated languages, and &#123;&#123;<a href="/wiki/Template:IPA" title="Template:IPA">IPA</a>&#125;&#125; for phonetic transcriptions, with an appropriate <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_ISO_639_codes" title="Lists of ISO 639 codes">ISO 639 code</a>. Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Category:Wikipedia_multilingual_support_templates" title="Category:Wikipedia multilingual support templates">multilingual support templates</a> may also be used.<span class="hide-when-compact"> <a href="/wiki/Template:Lang#Rationale" title="Template:Lang">See why</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li>In the work <i>Skazanie izjavljenno o pismeneh</i> that was written between 1423 and 1426, the Bulgarian chronicler <a href="/wiki/Constantine_of_Kostenets" title="Constantine of Kostenets">Constantine the Philosopher</a>, in parallel with the Bulgarian, Serbian, Slovenian, Czech and Croatian, he also mentions the Bosnian language.<sup id="cite_ref-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_6_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_6-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The notary book of the town of Kotor from July 3, 1436, recounts a duke buying a girl that is described as a: "Bosnian woman, heretic and in the Bosnian language called Djevena".<sup id="cite_ref-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_6_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_6-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The work <i>Thesaurus Polyglottus</i>, published in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt am Main</a> in 1603 by the German historian and linguist <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_Megiser" title="Hieronymus Megiser">Hieronymus Megiser</a>, mentions the Bosnian dialect alongside the Dalmatian, Croatian and Serbian one.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Bosnian Franciscan <a href="/wiki/Matija_Divkovi%C4%87" title="Matija Divković">Matija Divković</a>, regarded as the founder of the modern literature of Bosnia and Herzegovina,<sup id="cite_ref-Lovrenovic_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lovrenovic-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hrvatska-rijec_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrvatska-rijec-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> asserts in his work <i>Nauk krstjanski za narod slovinski</i> ("The Christian doctrine for the Slavic peoples") from 1611 his "translation from Latin to the real and true Bosnian language" (<i>A privideh iz dijačkog u pravi i istinit jezik bosanski</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_24_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_24-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Bosniak poet and <a href="/wiki/Arebica" title="Arebica">Aljamiado</a> writer <a href="/wiki/Muhamed_Hevaji_Uskufi_Bosnevi" title="Muhamed Hevaji Uskufi Bosnevi">Muhamed Hevaji Uskufi Bosnevi</a> who refers to the language of his 1632 dictionary<i> Magbuli-arif</i> as Bosnian.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>One of the first grammarians, the Jesuit clergyman <a href="/wiki/Bartol_Ka%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Bartol Kašić">Bartolomeo Cassio</a> calls the language used in his work from 1640 <i>Ritual rimski</i> ('Roman Rite') as <i>naški</i> ('our language') or <i>bosanski</i> ('Bosnian'). He used the term "Bosnian" even though he was born in a <a href="/wiki/Chakavian" title="Chakavian">Chakavian</a> region: instead he decided to adopt a "common language" (<span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">lingua communis</i></span>) based on a version of <a href="/wiki/Shtokavian" title="Shtokavian">Shtokavian</a> <a href="/wiki/Ikavian" class="mw-redirect" title="Ikavian">Ikavian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_8_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_8-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vatroslav_Jagić_1948_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vatroslav_Jagić_1948-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Italian linguist <a href="/wiki/Jakov_Mikalja" title="Jakov Mikalja">Giacomo Micaglia</a> (1601–1654) who states in his dictionary <i>Blagu jezika slovinskoga</i> (<i>Thesaurus lingue Illyricae</i>) from 1649 that he wants to include "the most beautiful words" adding that "of all <a href="/wiki/Illyrian_movement" title="Illyrian movement">Illyrian</a> languages the Bosnian is the most beautiful", and that all Illyrian writers should try to write in that language.<sup id="cite_ref-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_8_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_8-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vatroslav_Jagić_1948_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vatroslav_Jagić_1948-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>18th century Bosniak chronicler <a href="/wiki/Mula_Mustafa_Ba%C5%A1eskija" title="Mula Mustafa Bašeskija">Mula Mustafa Bašeskija</a> who argues in his yearbook of collected Bosnian poems that the "Bosnian language" is much richer than the Arabic, because there are 45 words for the verb "to go" in Bosnian.<sup id="cite_ref-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_24_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muhsin_Rizvić_1996_24-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Venetian writer, naturalist and cartographer <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Fortis" title="Alberto Fortis">Alberto Fortis</a> (1741–1803) calls in his work <i><a href="/wiki/Viaggio_in_Dalmazia" title="Viaggio in Dalmazia">Viaggio in Dalmazia</a></i> ("Journey to Dalmatia") the language of <a href="/wiki/Morlachs" title="Morlachs">Morlachs</a> as Illyrian, Morlach and Bosnian.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Croatian writer and lexicographer <a href="/wiki/Matija_Petar_Katan%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Matija Petar Katančić">Matija Petar Katančić</a> published six volumes of biblical translations in 1831 described as being "transferred from Slavo-Illyrian to the pronunciation of the Bosnian language".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Croatian writer <a href="/wiki/Matija_Ma%C5%BEurani%C4%87" title="Matija Mažuranić">Matija Mažuranić</a> refers in the work <i>Pogled u Bosnu</i> (1842) to the language of Bosnians as Illyrian (a 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">synonym</a> to <a href="/wiki/South_Slavic_languages" title="South Slavic languages">South Slavic languages</a>) mixed with Turkish words, with a further statement that they are the speakers of the Bosniak language.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Bosnian Franciscan <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Franjo_Juki%C4%87" title="Ivan Franjo Jukić">Ivan Franjo Jukić</a> states in his work <i>Zemljopis i Poviestnica Bosne</i> (1851) that Bosnia was the only Turkish land (i.e. under the control of the Ottoman Empire) that remained entirely pure without Turkish speakers, both in the villages and so on the highlands. Further he states "[...] a language other than the Bosnian is not spoken [in Bosnia], the greatest Turkish [i.e. Muslim] gentlemen only speak Turkish when they are at the <a href="/wiki/Vizier" title="Vizier">Vizier</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Kukuljevi%C4%87_Sakcinski" title="Ivan Kukuljević Sakcinski">Ivan Kukuljević Sakcinski</a>, a 19th-century Croatian writer and historian, stated in his work <i>Putovanje po Bosni (Travels into Bosnia)</i> from 1858, how the 'Turkish' (i.e. Muslim) Bosniaks, despite converting to the Muslim faith, preserved their traditions and the Slavic mood, and that they speak the purest variant of the Bosnian language, by refusing to add Turkish words to their vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span id="Differences_between_Bosnian.2C_Croatian_and_Serbian"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_between_Bosnian,_Croatian_and_Serbian">Differences between Bosnian, Croatian and Serbian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Differences between Bosnian, Croatian and Serbian"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_standard_Bosnian,_Croatian,_Montenegrin_and_Serbian" title="Comparison of standard Bosnian, Croatian, Montenegrin and Serbian">Comparison of standard Bosnian, Croatian, Montenegrin and Serbian</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian_phonology" title="Serbo-Croatian phonology">Serbo-Croatian phonology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian_grammar" title="Serbo-Croatian grammar">Serbo-Croatian grammar</a></div>
<p>The differences between the Bosnian, Serbian, and Croatian literary standards are minimal. Although Bosnian employs more <a href="/wiki/List_of_Serbo-Croatian_words_of_Turkish_origin" title="List of Serbo-Croatian words of Turkish origin">Turkish, Persian, and Arabic loanwords</a>—commonly called orientalisms—mainly in its spoken variety due to the fact that most Bosnian speakers are Muslims, it is still very similar to both Serbian and Croatian in its written and spoken form.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> "Lexical differences between the ethnic variants are extremely limited, even when compared with those between closely related Slavic languages (such as standard Czech and Slovak, Bulgarian and Macedonian), and grammatical differences are even less pronounced. More importantly, complete understanding between the ethnic variants of the standard language makes translation and second language teaching impossible."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bosnian language, as a new normative register of the Shtokavian dialect, was officially introduced in 1996 with the publication of <i><span title="Bosnian-language text"><i lang="bs">Pravopis bosanskog jezika</i></span></i> in Sarajevo. According to that work, Bosnian differed from Serbian and Croatian on some main linguistic characteristics, such as: sound formats in some words, especially "h" (<span title="Bosnian-language text"><i lang="bs">kahva</i></span> versus Serbian <span title="Serbian-language text"><i lang="sr">kafa</i></span>); substantial and deliberate usage of Oriental ("Turkish") words; spelling of future tense (<span title="Bosnian-language text"><i lang="bs">kupit ću</i></span>) as in Croatian but not Serbian (<span title="Serbian-language text"><i lang="sr">kupiću</i></span>) (both forms have the same pronunciation).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESotirović201448_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESotirović201448-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2019)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 2018, in the new issue of <span title="Bosnian-language text"><i lang="bs">Pravopis bosanskog jezika</i></span>, words without "h" are accepted due to their prevalence in language practice.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sample text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Article 1 of the <i><a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a></i> in Bosnian, written in the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic script</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><i>Сва људска бића рађају се слободна и једнака у достојанству и правима. Она су обдарена разумом и свијешћу и треба да једно према другоме поступају у духу братства.</i></dd></dl>
<p>Article 1 of the <i>Universal Declaration of Human Rights</i> in Bosnian, written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><i>Sva ljudska bića rađaju se slobodna i jednaka u dostojanstvu i pravima. Ona su obdarena razumom i sviješću i treba da jedno prema drugome postupaju u duhu bratstva.</i></dd></dl>
<p>Article 1 of the <i>Universal Declaration of Human Rights</i> in English:<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><i>All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood.</i></dd></dl>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Cyrillic-note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Cyrillic-note_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Cyrillic-note_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Cyrillic is an officially recognized alphabet, but in practice it is mainly used in <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a>, whereas in the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> mainly Latin is used.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlexander20061–2_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlexander20061–2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></span>
